* I merely refer to it as an experience which I have had and which appears to me to be <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> against a section of our community. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* Whether or not this can be proved or whether or not it is true I am unable to say at this stage but I became aware of what appeared to me to be an example of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> within our Australian community. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I have heard allegations of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> against the Aboriginal community by various other sections of our society; of exploitation carried out over the counters of shops, and exploitation by people involved in the delivery business. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I recall other stories of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in the field of employment particularly as it applied to apprentices. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* These could be expanded maybe but it becomes, as honourable senators would very well know, difficult to prove that a situation of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> occurs. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* In the outline of the allegations and in the observations it has been presented to me as a member of the Senate Committee that there was a section of our Australian community that was suffering some disadvantage that it should not have suffered; that there was a section of our Australian community that felt that it was being discriminated against and was offended or hurt as a result of this <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> which it believed it was not entitled to receive. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I think it also should be mentioned that there is a growing number of people within our Australian community- there is a growing number of communities within Australiawho are seriously concerned, as have been speakers in this debate, about racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in Australia and who through the various opportunities available to them are doing constructive work to combat <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I think of Aboriginal legal services and of various schools and colleges within our Australian community, but more particularly I pay tribute to individual citizens, privately and those who are involved in public affairs, who take upon themselves very seriously tasks and opportunities to rid the country of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and particularly to serve people who may feel that they have been victims of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* This is not good for society, certainly is not good for the people concerned and might very well be described as a form of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* Indeed, in my thinking it is the most effective way to destroy racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I am a little reluctant but I do mention that it is a matter of regret and indeed grief to some groups within our society that the Baltic community in Australia still has a very strong feeling that it has been the victim of some <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, so that when we undertake legislation here, whether it be the Government or the whole Senate, in connection with the matter of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, I think we have to be aware of the complexities that exist and aware of the fact that even the most finely developed legislation cannot solve all of the human and the personal problems in racial matters. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* If Australia is successfully to face the challenge of the next decade and in particular to solve its present problems it cannot afford the self destroying tendency to <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> which unfortunately exists within the community. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* While I acknowledge that the Bill seeks the goal of removing racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, I question sometimes in my mind whether it over emphasises the legal remedies to these problems as compared with other remedies. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I refer to educating people against racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> particularly as a long term solution. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* On the one hand there is freedom of expression and on the other hand the protection of the individual against <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* Therefore I feel, looking at clause 31 again, that systematic and extensive programs of community education may in the long run very well be the most effective way of creating and maintaining a harmonious social environment that is free from <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I merely cite it as an example as one way in which if not a knowledge of a language at least an appreciation of a language would help in this matter of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I believe, to be perfectly true, that legislation, worthy though it may be, cannot guarantee to heal racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I rise to support the second reading of the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Bill 1975 and also to support, at the same time, the amendments which the Liberal and National Country Parties will be proposing. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* We are, of course, discussing a Bill which involves primarily and firstly the ratification of an international convention relating to the elimination of all forms of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* The Bill concerns racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in the broad sense in which it is interpreted in Article 1 of the Convention, namely, distinction, exclusion, restriction or preference based upon race, colour, descent or national or ethnic origin. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* We have seen 81 countries ratify or accede to the International Convention on the Elimination of all Forms of Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* Some of my colleagues have said that this is not perhaps the worst country in the world for racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, that this is certainly a country with its tradition of freedom that ought to be in the forefront of those that proclaim freedom from racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and that set a lead to other countries. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* When the subject was debated in the House of Representatives, there was a general unity of purpose on the part of members on both sides of the chamber and many were the illustrations of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in this country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* Because of these problems, once again created by governments, we are now faced with this Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* In my opinion, if this Bill is implemented it will create more <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, not less. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* In other words, he takes the Bill as being totally unsatisfactory because it will in his opinion increase the <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> that exists in this country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* Far from eliminating racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> by making it illegal, the Bill will highlight the problems between the races and create an official race relations industry with a staff of dedicated anti-racists earning their living by making the most of every complaint in much the same way as does the Race Relations Board in the United Kingdom. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I would have thought that that was an obvious statement but, at the same time, racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> is here. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I say there is <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in this country against migrants not only in respect of words but also in respect of jobs. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I say to  Senator Wood  that the expectation that they must speak our language is one of the indications of our <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> against these people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* If he means by that that those people will realise that there is <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> against them and that they have a remedy, I think it is a good thing that they shall have a remedy, that they shall not continue to live in that state but will be able to improve their position in life. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* When it was drawn to his attention that they still suffer <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in this country, he preferred to say that that sort of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> brings the best out of people and that if they dig deep into themselves when they are discriminated against that is the way they improve their morale. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I do not know how one should regard the extremes of Hitler in that regard but I do not believe that <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> is a desirable thing for the purpose of improving the morale of people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I do not accept that type of explanation and excuse for racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in this country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* If I were dealing with 3 wise monkeys I suppose that he would be the one who could see no evil because he has had a fortunate life of innocence in which he has never accepted that there is racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in this country. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* He said: 'I am not prepared to admit that there is that pocket of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in this country'. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* When  Senator Cavanagh  said that there were pockets of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>,  Senator Bunton  said that there was not even that. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I think we all know, as has been established in this debate, that there are serious realms of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* The honourable senator has not read the Bill because the definition of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in the Bill includes national <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and ethnic <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* These are matters of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and are dealt with by this Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* Consequently, in reply to  Senator Bunton  who said that he is not aware of blatant racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in this country, I put it to him that some of the worst forms of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> are those that are not even known or appreciated by people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* It does not matter whether the <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> is blatant or not. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* It is obvious that the common law has never developed in such a way that it would eliminate racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* The existing rights and remedies are costly and difficult to deal with racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I think the procedure includes no way of removing fortunately- nor does the Convention- that benign <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, that ability to assist people who are below the average in their standards of living or in their rights and privileges and whose standard may be brought up under the provisions of this Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* In respect of this matter I would like to read the words of the Director of the Ontario Human Rights Commission who explained what was done in relation to his body's conciliation approach to racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* The same applies even more so in the case of statements on racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* It is in that respect that the Convention is somewhat obscure because, although it does call upon nations to make punishable by law the offence of the dissemination of ideas based upon racial superiority or hatred, the Convention also says that each State Party shall prohibit and bring to an end, by all appropriate means including legislation as required by the circumstances, racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> by all persons, groups or organisations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* Under the innocuous badge of banning racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> the Labor Party has introduced the apparatus of the Police State, with its secret Police, empowered to engage in inquisitorial investigations, fines, imprisonment, arrest, damages and injunctions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* one remarks that this ' Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Bill ' was drawn up in its present form largely by a man of southern European origins and with a southern European temperament assisted, so he said, by a woman of southern European origins who was reared in eastern Asia and the Philippines . [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I have mixed feelings about it because for so many years of my life I have known racial prejudice and <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* To my consternation, to my hurt and to my shame I have found throughout this country <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and prejudice aimed particularly at one of the minority groups. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* Some have said that there is no <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I say to all and sundry: Ask an Italian, a Sicilian, or a Greek who has been called, to use some of the denigrating terms that have been used, a wop or a greaser or ask a Jew who has been called a hooknose or a moneybags whether he knows what <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> is. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* There is <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and we must do something about it. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* No more <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> against those who are less fortunate in the community, those who have a different coloured skin, those who speak a different tongue or those who are not so well educated. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* There is no <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, according to some people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* Because of past <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and things that have happened in the past, a group of young Aboriginal men and women could become angry, and outside this place they could shout, 'Down with the whitey ', or something about some race of people. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* It is of some interest to note that in the calendar year 1972 a total of 908 complaints were made to the Race Relations Board and that the Board formed the opinion that there had been some <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in 181 of those cases. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* One sees that in relation to only one category of complaints disposed of in that period of 5 full years did the Board, after investigation, make a finding of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in more than 30 per cent of the cases in the category. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I was somewhat surprised to find that eventually they were prepared to say that they believed it was more properly a matter of human rights than a matter of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in the approach which should be adopted. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I have always wondered whether our approach may not be better if we were not to emphasise racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> as though it were the only form of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> that mattered but rather to concentrate on ensuring the human rights of all Australian citizens in relation to racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> or any other form of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* As is well known, this Bill introduces into Australian law obligations contained in the International Convention for the Elimination of All Forms of Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* In any event, I got an impression in listening to  Senator Greenwood  in this debate that he was a reluctant supporter of a Bill to outlaw racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, and I hasten to add that I am not attempting to overstate the case. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* I do not for one moment believe that  Senator Greenwood  is in favour of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750527_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-54-0)

* One of the greatest problems which we face is the <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> by and the attitudes of some of these unions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#subdebate-37-0)

* I ask the Minister for Manufacturing Industry  (Senator James McClelland)  whether it is intended to apply to the relevant authorities for the International Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> to be ratified and whether that application is to be made forthwith. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* The International Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> came into force as a convention in 1 969. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* The first difficulty which comes to mind is that, on a reading of the Australian Constitution, the power to make laws about racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> seems to rest with the States. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* There is certainly no express power in the Commonwealth Parliament to make laws with respect to the outlawing of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* I refer the Minister to Article 4 which provides that adherents to the Convention are to 'condemn all propaganda and all organisations which are based on ideas or theories of superiority of one race or group of persons of one colour or ethnic origin, or which attempt to justify or promote racial hatred and <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in any form, and undertake to adopt immediate and positive measures designed to eradicate all incitement to, or acts of, such <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>'. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* For example, there is a requirement to declare an offence punishable by law all dissemination of ideas based on racial superiority or hatred, incitement to racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, as well as all acts of violence or incitement to such acts. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* There is also an obligation to declare illegal and to prohibit organisations and also organised and all other propaganda activities which promote and incite racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* Whatever one might say about ideas based on racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, just as one might say a lot of things about other social or political tenets to which one can express abhorrence, in this country we have endeavoured to provide as much free speech as we can. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* They challenge freedom of speech on the justification, presumably, that such steps are necessary to abolish racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* We have seen in the United Nations how in the name of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> countries like Rhodesia and South Africa have been treated as pariahs and have been excluded from the world community. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* Other countries which practise racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> are lauded in the United Nations and are permitted to condemn other countries while their own conduct remains unexamined. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* That means that the constitutional limitations, the general juristic limitations, on our power to deal with racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in this country will be considered by that Committee in considering as a result of complaints whether we have complied with the terms of the Convention. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* The fact that we are attempting to deal with matters of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in this country does not affect the fact that people who consider themselves to be aggrieved by our laws will avail themselves of their freedom to criticise us. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* If we are to appear in the eyes of the world as a country which abhors racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, and which does what it can to eliminate racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, we just have to cop it sweet, to use a good old Australian expression. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* A nonracist society or a society which is trying to eliminate racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> is, I suggest, a society which can stand such criticism and which can say: 'We stand on our record and we are doing what we can to eliminate racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. ' [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* The scheme of the Bill is that in clauses 11, 12, 13, 14, 15 and 16 there are a number of activities which are declared to be unlawful if they take place by reason of an act of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, as that expression is used throughout those clauses. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* What is the greater offence in the field of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> was practised by people infected with the anti-semitic virus. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* I do not see anything illogical or inconsistent in the proposition that it is more evil to incite to racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> than to practise acts of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* Also, there is the technical matter that the Convention does require us to make incitement to racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> a criminal offence. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* But, if there is the provision of services or the selling of a house and the employee or the agent commits an act of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in the performance of his duties, then that is the commission of an act that is unlawful. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* He said that the barman would be free from the charge of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> if the owner was proved to have told the barman that he must not serve drinks to this type or colour of person. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750528_senate_29_s64/#debate-38)

* To use the Minister's example, if a barman commits an act which is unlawful because it is an act of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, he must face the consequences which this legislation imposes. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* -Prior to the suspension of the sitting I was indicating that there can be 2 reasons why an act alleged to be an act of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> has occurred. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* Perhaps the person might also take a view based on racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* It might be that the racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> is a quite substantial element but not necessarily the dominant element. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* I refer to the South Australian Prohibition of <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act which put an extremely heavy onus on the complainant. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* I understand that that Act required a complainant to show that the <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> occurred by reason only of race, country of origin or colour of the skin. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* To require proof that the <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> occurred as a result of those reasons only is to cast a very heavy onus indeed on any complainant. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* If that is considered a wishy-washy point to make, I would refer to the sort of statistics quoted by  Senator Rae  in the second reading debate and to the statistics of the English Race Relations Commission which indicate that in that country, at least, a large number of cases are brought which are found not to be based on racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* The Commissioner has two types of fuction One is to promote an understanding and acceptance of the various programs and need for avoidance of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* In this area of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, where we are making a start in this country with regard to a comprehensive law of this character, we believe it is tremendously important to tread carefully and not in an over-zealous pursuit of enforcement powers to create the possibility of a backlash that would do more harm in the long run than good. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* This makes a travesty of the efforts of an authority like this to do something about stamping out racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* I share with nobody my detestation of ideas of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> based upon racial superiority or a <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> which seeks to evoke a superiority. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* I would prefer to see this clause removed entirely and I think that we do better in this area of trying to avoid racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, of allowing the free interplay of ideas, by hoping that the tolerance which ought to be current in this community to receive and listen to differing viewpoints, no matter how antipathetic they may be to us, will be encouraged and permitted. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* The provisions penalising these offences are entirely separate in character from the anti-<span class="highlight">discrimination</span> provisions of Part II of the Bill, and are enforced by separate machinery. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* Their inclusion in the Bill is likely to create, as it has in Britain, an ineradicable impression in the public mind that the whole Bill is concerned with the criminal courts, fines and imprisonment; the crucial element in the whole exercise, the tackling of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> by informal conciliation, may become de-emphasised; and public sympathy may tend to be directed more towards the discriminator, believed to be likely to receive harsh penalties, than his victim. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* In the minds of some people apparently this can cause a great feeling of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* It is a little bit tough for such people to be called up just because they say something or publish something that somebody regards as being racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* Where do we stop this <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> business? [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1975/19750529_senate_29_s64/#debate-41)

* In addition to this Act, the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act became effective in law from 31 October 1975. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760817_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-37-18)

* This Act has a more general application to <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> based on race, colour, descent or national or ethnic origin, and makes it unlawful for a person to do an act involving racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> which impairs the enjoyment, on an equal footing of fundamental rights and freedoms. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760817_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-37-18)

* This Act also contains provision which guarantees equality before the law in the enjoyment of rights without <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> based on race, and which are designed to supersede State or Commonwealth laws that discriminate on ground of race in relation to the enjoyment or rights. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760817_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-37-18)

* This Act also prescribes acts of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in respect of access to places and facilities available to members of the public, the disposal of land, housing and other accommodation, the provision of goods and services to the public, employment, and the right to join trade unions. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1976/19760817_senate_30_s69/#subdebate-37-18)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* That is the attitude of the Opposition to this Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill 1 979. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* There has been a proliferation of such machinery at both Federal and State levels in recent years, in the areas especially of racial and sexual <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>- if  Senator Maunsell  can bring himself for a moment to concentrate on concepts which will be entirely unfamiliar to him, I expect- and also in the area of privacy. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* I might add that similarly to try, as the Government apparently intends doing, to dismantle the national network of employment <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> committees, those tripartite bodies of employers, unions and government which have engaged very successfully in the - [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* That is a matter on which the Australian Council of Trade Unions, the Confederation of Australian Industry and the  Chairman  of the National Committee on <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> in Employment and Occupation,  Dr Colin  Hughes, remain quite unpersuaded. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* Given the fact that the responsibility for these communities at the moment is still tenuously within the Ministry of Employment, and possibly within the area of industrial relations- there seems to be some kind of tug of war going on in that particular area- those Ministers who have the most immediate responsibility for the administration of that particular informal anti-<span class="highlight">discrimination</span> operation have not made the position at all clear. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* In addition to the courts, I believe that it is appropriate and desirable that there should be enforcement mechanisms and enforcement machinery of an investigative, conciliatory kind, with which we have become familiar in the work of  Mr Grassby,  the Community Relations Commission, the various States' sexual <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and equal opportunity commissions and the Privacy Committee in New South Wales. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* It is not a substitute for other more specific, more piecemeal solutions to particular human rights problems in the privacy area, the sexual and racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> area, the criminal investigation area and other areas as well. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* The Human Rights Commission Bill and the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill, which are connected pieces of legislation, have been in gestation for quite a long time. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* I think that we can make alterations to the Human Rights Commission Bill which will turn the proposed Commission into an organisation which can be effective, but I do not see any way in which we can deal with the other Bill, the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill, which has been criticised so vehemently by  Senator Evans  this afternoon. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* Last year the Australian Government submitted to the World Conference to Combat Racism and Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> a national report which stated that action taken in this country to combat racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> had been based on five principles. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* Racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> should be made unlawful by specific legislation; [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* Formal administrative machinery should be established for the investigation of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> on a systematic basis and to attempt to settle issues involving <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> by conciliation; [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* A comprehensive framework of legally enforceable remedies should be created to provide redress against racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> where conciliation fails. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* I do not believe that we have adequately enforced that racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> covenant as yet. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* By  Senator Alan  Missen on the terms of the 1979 Human Rights Commission Bill and Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill (As introduced in the Senate on 25 September 1 979) [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* Unlike the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act 1975, the Bill does not formally approve ratification of the Covenant although the Government has expressed its desire for early ratification. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* The Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill is a complementary Bill which will transfer the functions, now performed by the Commissioner for Community Relations  (Dr [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* But individuals who may breach human rights (an employer, a Union or a publican for example) may be determined on a course of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and in no way susceptible to public or governmental pressure. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* Contrast this Bill with the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act, which provides various offences which may be prosecuted to ensure compliance with the 'International Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span>', which we ratified in 1973. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* The Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill ( 1979) [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* The Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act 197S was passed with the support of the ALP Government and the Liberal-Country [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* The Commissioner for Community Relations, who already has specific responsibilities in the area of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, is not named as a Human Rights Commissioner and it is clear to me that he will not be appointed to such a position. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* There is indeed a case for amalgamating the operations concerning racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> with other human rights (as the Galbally Report recommends), but not by downgrading the existing working operations of the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act and debarring its Commissioner from the policy determinations of the Commission. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* Bearing in mind the possibility of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> occurring in remote areas of the country, the contrasting power of delegation is significant. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* It will be noted that the powers over racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> now being transferred to the Commission are not 'toothless' but have been developed with limited facilities yet with overall success. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* No action should be taken, either by reason of personal animosities or for other reasons, to weaken the operation of the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act 1975, which was an all-party endorsement by the Commonwealth Parliament of an International Convention to control racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* I turn now to the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill because that is a Bill which amalgamates the operations which have been effectively going on for a number of years under [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* The Committee expresses its concern that the Human Rights Commission Bill and the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill, which are currently before Federal Parliament, would reduce the chance for such activities as those in Queensland to be documented and brought to the attention of the public. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* Before the suspension of sitting, I was dealing with what are in my opinion defects in the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* This is no time for us to make a major change in the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act when a challenge is about to be launched which will determine whether the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act is valid. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* He of course there seeks among other things the support of the Commonwealth Government in defending the challenge- in other words, in defending the right of the Commonwealth to have taken the action under the International Convention and to have proclaimed and to have operated the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act. * I take a fundamental view in regard to the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* I am not satisfied with the amount of expenditure on and the amount of staff employed in the area of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* I am certainly not satisfied that it is proposed to have sufficient staff to cover the whole operation of the Human Rights Commission plus the area of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, and that the staff will in any way be even as adequate as is presently existent for the Commissioner for Community Relations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* His two deputies are on loan from other Government departments, and all matters pertaining to racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> are handled by a skeletal staff: eight in the Canberra office and one representative in Melbourne and Sydney. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* The Commissioner has no representative in Western Australia, Queensland and the Northern Territory, where some of the worst instances of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> have been alleged. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* In view of the weaknesses of the Act, the limited scope allowed the Commissioner for Community Relations, the failure to establish either a Community Relations Office or Council on a statutory basis, and the reality of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in Australia, there are strong grounds for asking whether the Australian Government is serious in its commitment to fight for racial equality. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* I will oppose the passage of the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill because I believe it is contrary to what I have fought for in this Parliament and what I have voted for in this Parliament. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* I rise to address my remarks to the Human Rights Commission Bill and, to a much lesser extent, the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-65-0)

* I wonder whether the Government will have the courage also to ratify the optional protocol which it seems to me would allow individuals to appeal to the human rights committee set up as a consequence of Part IV of the principal Covenant in order to receive complaints from individuals about acts of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> by State parties which take place as far as they are concerned. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791108_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-77-2)

* -In my notable speech to the Senate last Thursday on the Human Rights Commission Bill 1979 and the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill 1979-1 will be concluding my speech with only a few short remarks- I pointed out the basis of my grave misgivings concerning the Government's good faith even in presenting this human rights legislation to this Parliament. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* I join the debate on the Human Rights Commission Bill 1 979 and the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill 1979. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* The Government will perhaps accomplish with the Bill in its present form another toothless tiger such as the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act 1975. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* In most of these cases, particularly where racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> or breaches of human rights occur, it is the most unfortunate people, economically, educationally and in other ways, who would not have the wherewithal to be able to carry out that kind of prosecution. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* I believe that the areas which will fall within the province of the Commonwealth will be negligible, as presently State laws cover most of the areas in which breaches of human rights and <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> occur. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* That would be rather ludicrous because it is under State laws, particularly in my State, that most of the <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> against Aboriginal people occurs. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* I believe that such a provision is completely unacceptable if we are to have fair dinkum legislation in relation to human rights and racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* All he wants to do is to be free from that kind of attitude, that kind of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and that kind of oppression. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* I believe that in both these pieces of legislation there should be provision for prosecutions for breaches of human rights, regardless of the kind of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> there may be against a person or persons. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* I have said time and time again that in relation to stamping out <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act of 1975 has always seemed to me to be a toothless tiger as I have always felt that in most instances <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> is a state of mind, an inherent belief, which can be eliminated only by reason, greater knowledge, tolerance and understanding. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* I am confining most of my remarks to the racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> aspects of these two Bills. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* I say that because I disagree with the amendments to the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act which will bring the Commissioner for Community Relations under the new Commission. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* He will have no way of doing things on his own behalf, as he has been doing by travelling around the country and setting up in different towns voluntary organisations of groups of people who are interested in looking into acts of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* The Senate, in debating the issues of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and human rights, is really beginning to concern itself about democracy and about the interpretation of democracy as it is applied. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* The demand for legislation to deal with racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and human rights is synonymous with demands that are being made in many countries in the world. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* That is why earlier I referred to the <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> that existed and the power that, because of the way in which our society is structured, flowed from that <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* There is a need to recognise the deficiencies that exist in the society and the need for some public debate, some legislative action, and some better understanding within the community about the power disposition, the power <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and the inequality that that brings to the average person in the Australian community. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* I am not suggesting that Australia is any different from any other country, because I think what we have witnessed in recent times is this tremendous world movement towards human rights and against <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, and the struggle of the Third World countries to be recognised in the same way as other countries, the realisation that the superpowers should not have the sort of powers that they have to make decisions over life and death, peace and war. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* They put it to  Senator Murphy  and me that we should come down on a Friday night to have a look at what happens in the pubs around Redfern, and that they should show us exactly how the law operates in terms of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> against the human rights of blacks. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* Of course, we know that this form of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> which takes place within the States themselves has been a running sore for a considerable number of years. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* It is a form of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, and yet this legislation does nothing to overcome the obstinacy and the refusal of State governments to come into line on the question of human rights and against racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* So while the Opposition recognises the tentative step that this Government has taken in this legislation, we nevertheless feel that it is purely a first step in a very long march towards an understanding of human rights and ending racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* Complaints have come from civil liberty groups, employer groups, church groups, the United Nations Association of Australia, trade unions, a number of important citizens in our community and people in the legal fraternity who know what <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> means because they have to deal with the rough side of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> almost every day in the law courts. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* It is under State laws that <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> finds its reflection. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* It is under State laws that Aborigines are discriminated against and it is under State laws that there is <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> against women. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* We have not moved that far in terms of evolution and technological change when we still have areas of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> within society. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* We all know, if we know anything of the way officialdom has dealt with the problems of Aborigines in the back-blocks of Australia, that the person at the level of making the decision is the one who often practices the <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* If one has a problem of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, it has to be examined to see why that power is exerted in such a way to create the act of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> is created because it is inherent in the very system in which we live. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* To suggest that we should enact legislation at the Commonwealth level without following it through right down the line in a way that makes the practising of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and denial of human rights an offence is to forsake our responsibilities. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* The theories of democracy and the way democracy operates ought to be examined in the light of the thousands and thousands of cases of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> that appear. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* That will give some nebulous group or person the opportunity to make it even more difficult for the ordinary citizen to become involved in an inquiry when he or she suffers from <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* To say that it is more than that would be to gild the lily very considerably because this legislation will not put an end to racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* We have an obligation to define the areas of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and the areas in which human rights are threatened and prejudiced as a result of the way our society operates. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

* Apart from the Attorney-General  (Senator Durack),  I am the eighth senator to speak- there have been four speakers from the Opposition side and four from the Government benches- and so far everyone except the Attorney-General has criticised the Human Rights Commission Bill 1 979 and the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill 1 979. * Under the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-73-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#debate-75)

* The only other matter I wish to mention relates to the proposed amendments to the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-75-0)

[[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791113_senate_31_s83/#subdebate-75-0)

* Will the Attorney-General tell the Senate whether he has received from Amnesty International, the United Nations Associations, civil liberties organisations and other bodies submissions in connection with the Human Rights Commission Bill and the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill which have not yet been debated in the Senate? * Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* Honourable senators will recall that that Bill has the effect of incorporating the racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> administration under  Mr Grassby  in the operations of the Human Rights Commission but does not make him a commissioner of the Human Rights Commission. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* The effect of that is that one member of the Commission, which is to consist of a  chairman,  a  deputy chairman  and not less than five nor more than nine other members, would already have been already identified as the person who holds the rank and office, under the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act, of Commissioner for Community Relations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* This has been a proved and tried method under the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* Under the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill which has yet to be discussed in detail,  Mr Grassby  is to be under the direction of the Human Rights Commission. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* Under the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill, no opportunity will be presented for him to have a separate staff, but he would be in a position to argue the need for such staff if he were a commissioner. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* It meets the requirement that we should not in any way turn the racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> administration into a defective organisation; that we should not create a situation in which there will be a clash between the Human Rights Commission and the Commissioner for Community Relations. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* For these reasons I have moved this amendment, which I regard as extremely important to the continuing operation of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> oversight and the most effective working of the Human Rights Commission. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* It is a matter for great regret that the vote to reject the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill was lost last night only by one vote, as a result of the indavertent non-appearance in the chamber, in time, of  Senator Harradine. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* He has made it clear that he does not include within the range of his ambitions the employment <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> committees which now operate at the national level and at every State level. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* It is obvious that a consideration of this kind is at best a barely veiled rationalisation of the Government's real reason; that is, it finds  Mr Grassby,  the present Commissioner, a political embarrassment not because of his previous party affiliations but because of the way he so relentlessly exposed the deficiency of governmental activity both at the State and Federal levels in protecting our citizens against racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* As I said in my speech at the second reading stage, it is no accident that in the corridors of this Parliament back bench Liberal members are referring to the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill as the Get Grassby Bill', because that is what it is about. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* Under the provisions of the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill, which had its second reading last night, the various powers vested in the Commissioner are now to be taken from him and formally vested in the Commission. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* It is further obvious from the provisions of the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill that  Mr Grassby  will no longer have the right or the duty to prepare and deliver reports to the Parliament. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* It has sought to pretend and claim to the community at large that nothing is changing, that something is being added to the present structure for the protection of human rights, but that nothing is being taken away and that it is business as usual as far as the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act and  Mr Grassby  are concerned. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* It seems ludicrous to me that we are setting up the Human Rights Commission and that part and parcel of that Commission will be the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act under which the person holding the office of the Commissioner for Community Relations is to work. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* I am giving my total support to this amendment because I believe it is necessary, if we are to have Human Rights Commission and if we are to maintain the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act and the Office of the Commissioner for Community Relations, that the Commissioner have a vital role to play on that Commission. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* If the Human Rights Commission Bill and the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill are passed, that valuable body of experience, going back many years, will be embodied only in the person of the Commissioner. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* However, if somebody else were to be appointed to that position, I must say that I think that person, if he were a person of great integrity and great capacity, probably would want to think twice about taking a position which potentially was of such subservience as these Bills, the Human Rights Commission Bill and the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Amendment Bill, would reduce it to. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* I believe that the support which both sides of the Parliament gave to the original Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act indicates that. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* I believe that the support given to it in its eventual form by distinguished former Liberal senators, such as the late Ivor Greenwood, and the way in which he linked the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act with the first statutory reference to the International Covenant, indicate the seriousness with which honourable senators on this side of the Parliament have regarded the problems of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* It has been stressed each year that lack of resources in personnel and finance have made it impossible to make the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act 1975 and its provisions widely known and more readily accessible. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* As the Aboriginal population of Australia becomes progressively more and more educated and articulate it will find more and more that it is subject to acts of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> and that it is the object of positive prejudice by other Australian citizens and by governments. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* Appendix B on page 139 of the Commissioner's report shows that 238 of the 993 complaints that he dealt with last yearoverwhelmingly the largest number; in fact twice as large as any other individual group singled out- concerned complaints of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> against Aboriginals. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* The Commissioner, at chapter 9 of his report, which is headed <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> in Employment', says: [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* If honourable senators look at the figures in Appendix B as to why the Polish communities, for instance, should be singled out for <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> they will see the extent to which that is economically based. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* I direct the attention of honourable senators to those criticisms- the criticism that the Commissioner is placed under the control of the Human Rights Commission, that complaints will not be as easily handled by the Commissioner in the future, that he will be subject to directions that his access to staff will be reduced, that his report to Parliament will disappear and that his role in promoting an understanding and a public awareness of racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> matters will also disappear. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* He is aware, this Government is aware and the Labor Government was aware of the necessity to ensure that racial <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> in Australia is treated as the sort of community disease that it is and that actions are taken in order to prevent the spread of the disease and to excise the cancer of the disease whenever that is possible. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* It is in this period that the Government and the Parliament have to accept the responsibility of providing a framework so that those affected by the <span class="highlight">discrimination</span> that is taking place every day in every facet of our society can ventilate their complaints and experiences in a way that they feel will be understood and in a way that makes them feel part of the Australian community. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* He must be capable of seeking out and encouraging people discriminated against to believe that they have an avenue by which they can ventilate their problems and the acts of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* But it is in these areas where much of the <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, based upon the whole historical development of our country takes place. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* My father can tell me of countless instances of <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>, cruelty and barbarism on the part of the people at the turn of the century and right up to World War I. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* In the period that lies ahead, as indeed in the period that we are talking about, that experience, that understanding, that safety valve which are available there are at the moment to those disadvantaged people in our community, should be available to those who are suffering <span class="highlight">discrimination</span>; they should have the opportunity of appealing to this person. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)

* It so happens that at the moment we do have a Commissioner for Community Relations appointed under the Racial <span class="highlight">Discrimination</span> Act. [[More&hellip;]](https://historichansard.net/senate/1979/19791114_senate_31_s83/#debate-64)
